  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4c23dff1-eb3d-464c-8f0b-27338b4a740b'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">[The reason his other senses increased was because he was blind. When any animal becomes blind, it's senses increase to make up for the loss in sight.<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">[The reason his other senses increased was because he was blind. When any animal becomes blind, it's senses increase to make up for the loss in sight. That's why blind people have better hearing than people who can see.]<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5222564-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302651637p2/5222564.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168540810?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/5222564-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5222564-scott?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168540810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8213010458481159617">The title says an awful lot in this 2nd part of the Power of Three saga. It becomes more clear that Brambleclaw and Squirrelflight's kits are the three referenced in this series. There are many subtleties alluded to throughout this book but many tales are intertwined as the powers of Hollypaw (sense of diplomacy) and Lionpaw (skills as a tactician) begin to emerge. Sadly, another encounter with TigerStar, this time through Lionpaw, seems to give the power-hungry ancestor a new hold on ThunderCla</span>
  <span id="freeText8213010458481159617" style="display:none">The title says an awful lot in this 2nd part of the Power of Three saga. It becomes more clear that Brambleclaw and Squirrelflight's kits are the three referenced in this series. There are many subtleties alluded to throughout this book but many tales are intertwined as the powers of Hollypaw (sense of diplomacy) and Lionpaw (skills as a tactician) begin to emerge. Sadly, another encounter with TigerStar, this time through Lionpaw, seems to give the power-hungry ancestor a new hold on ThunderClan's destiny. However, we see that Brambleclaw appears to have at least a minor suspicion of his son's fighting strategy style and I can foresee a potential conflict building in the future. After all, the next title in the series is "Outcast" which already has me wondering and predicting.<br /><br />I think my favorite part of this chapter, however, was the growth of Jaypaw, especially as he learns to walk with his ancestors showing a bit more understanding, empathy, and maturity. The little kit is growing up and, while still not entirely comfortable with his set of life's circumstances, gives hope that he is indeed destined for great things. A little shout out to my friend, Micheline, for encouraging me to give Jaypaw's character another chance ... she was definitely right in keeping the faith!<br /><br />As always, now I can't wait to get started on the next book in the series and find out exactly what "Outcast" refers to ...</span>
  <a data-text-id="8213010458481159617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_159697266" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159697266" />
    <a title="Micheline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4845030-micheline"><img alt="Micheline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520260852p2/4845030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159697266?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Micheline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Micheline" href="/user/show/4845030-micheline">Micheline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=creature-characters">creature-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer159697266&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159697266" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10322447459311035900">Dark River is the 2nd book in the Power of Three (PO3) series of Warriors. It picks up precisely where PO3 #1, The Sight left off. As the title suggests, this book has a strong theme of looming darkness, or impending danger. An eminent battle threatens to put many clans in danger, and once again TigerStar'S presence is felt from beyond the grave. In The Sight, TigerStar & HawkFrost both approached JayPaw in a dream, and attempted to lure him into darkness, but he trusted his instinct and refused</span>
  <span id="freeText10322447459311035900" style="display:none">Dark River is the 2nd book in the Power of Three (PO3) series of Warriors. It picks up precisely where PO3 #1, The Sight left off. As the title suggests, this book has a strong theme of looming darkness, or impending danger. An eminent battle threatens to put many clans in danger, and once again TigerStar'S presence is felt from beyond the grave. In The Sight, TigerStar &amp; HawkFrost both approached JayPaw in a dream, and attempted to lure him into darkness, but he trusted his instinct and refused. This time around, TigerStar &amp; HawkFrost approach LionPaw, and offer to help him battle train at a perfect moment, and teach him valuable moves....and LionPaw seems willing to accept their help, only BrambleClaw seems to be weary, or suspect TigerStar's involvement....and he would know better than anyone.<br /><br />All 3 of FireStar's descendants, or BrambleClaw and SquirrelFlight's kits have secrets in this book, and its still hard to tell what their intentions are, or how they will eventually handle their ever growing powers. In 'The Signt', JayPaw's powers were the only ones I really noticed, and while his powers seem to be growing while growing more complicated, HollyPaw and LionPaw's powers seem to be coming into focus in this book. As usual, I cannot wait to see what happens next, another riveting addition to the Warriors series! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10322447459311035900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062367099" href="/book/show/23367398-dark-river">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37293133-kate-matson?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37293133-kate-matson?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37293133-kate-matson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1597384218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17104101528484648328">Summary:<br/>With more experience comes both power and danger: Lionpaw makes a friendship--and a discovery--that must be kept hidden; Jaypaw learns a secret that could benefit ThunderClan by damaging others; and Hollypaw knows something that could avert a battle, if she could convince the rest of her Clan.<br/>The three are torn apart as each discovers darkness: in themselves, in the Clans, and in the past. And, as conflict begins over what it means to be a warrior, rising tensions threaten to overflow, w</span>
  <span id="freeText17104101528484648328" style="display:none">Summary:<br />With more experience comes both power and danger: Lionpaw makes a friendship--and a discovery--that must be kept hidden; Jaypaw learns a secret that could benefit ThunderClan by damaging others; and Hollypaw knows something that could avert a battle, if she could convince the rest of her Clan.<br />The three are torn apart as each discovers darkness: in themselves, in the Clans, and in the past. And, as conflict begins over what it means to be a warrior, rising tensions threaten to overflow, washing away the peace that has existed for many moons. <br />Plot:<br />For some reason, so far the plot in The Power of Three series hasn't been as good as the rest. I know for a fact that it'll get better, but it's torture waiting. There's a main prophecy that I'm waiting to come into action, which I know it will in Outcast, the next book. I speed-read this book, which made it so much faster, therefore I was rarely bored. <br />Characters:<br />Jaypaw's attitude hasn't gotten much better, but at least he's a little nicer. In the first book, I didn't like Jaypaw at all, but now that I've seen more of his powers, I've come to respect him a little more. <br />Now onto Lionpaw. Lionpaw is great and all, but he's not an original character yet. He's basically the classic warrior that wants to become clan leader. I did, however, really like his relationship with Heatherpaw. <br />Hollypaw wasn't really featured that much in this book. She didn't play an important part in Dark River, she was basically just there to fill the 3 P.O.V. standards for this series. <br />Overall &amp; Recommendations:<br />Despite my complaints above, this was a great book. Definitely not the best warrior book, but it was still really good. I had my problems with the characters, but not much more. The entire Warrior series is amazing, and I recommend to all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17104101528484648328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15031592327682570599" style="display:none">Dark River by Erin Hunter is about the Tribes getting hostile over territory so the three and a few other cats find some lost kittens to stop the fighting. I really injoyed this book. First off one negative (and this might be a little petty but it still bothered me) is that Squirrelflights personality changed a bit. I know this was probably done intentionally (since she probably just wants to raise the kits as best as possible) but I think it was changed in the wrong way. She makes sure Hollypaw is perfectly obedient to the idea of apprentices being not able to think for themselves and tells her she'll just come around to the idea of having kits. I feel like she would be more energetic and kinda… softer I guess but she just seems out of character (in a really wrong way). But everything else (at least that I can remember since I have really bad memory) I found intriguing and fun to read about. I love Fallen Leaves so much. I recommend this book to anyone that likes cats. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer482957911159493534">Trouble is brewing and it seems as if the Clans are ready to battle each other. Hollypaw seems to think she can help. She questions why the Clans cannot help each other and disobeys Firestar to find answers to her questions. Meanwhile Lionpaw, her brother, has his own problems as he shares a secret with Heatherpaw, a River Clan apprentice. He also seems to have visions which as a warrior apprentice he should not have so why is he? Jaypaw, their brother who is the Medicine Cat apprentice, is havi</span>
  <span id="freeText482957911159493534" style="display:none">Trouble is brewing and it seems as if the Clans are ready to battle each other. Hollypaw seems to think she can help. She questions why the Clans cannot help each other and disobeys Firestar to find answers to her questions. Meanwhile Lionpaw, her brother, has his own problems as he shares a secret with Heatherpaw, a River Clan apprentice. He also seems to have visions which as a warrior apprentice he should not have so why is he? Jaypaw, their brother who is the Medicine Cat apprentice, is having visions but does not always know what to do with what he told by Star Clan. He finds a stick on the border but does not know why it whispers to him. He knows he must save and protect the stick without understanding why.<br /><br />I love this series. This particular series has me in its grasp since the first day I picked it up. I want to know what is going on and why these three seem to be involved so much as they are only apprentices. I know it will be something big and important. I cannot wait to find out what it is and if the Clans will work together or fight. The other Clans want to believe Thunder Clan is weak but Thunder Clan is stronger than the others because they are more tolerant and more willing to work together to help others.<br /><br />This is an excellent series as it teaches without preaching and has a lot of action and adventure as well as the history of the Clans.</span>

  <span id="freeText14068841115092387789" style="display:none">I struggled with this audiobook due to my health while listening, and it is therefore hard to rate, as I have no real, full grasp of the book as a whole.<br /><br />Jaypaw is finally becoming less of an annoyance, so yay, character growth! On the other hand, Hollypaw is getting on my nerves, and I want to yell at Lionpaw because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[dammit this is Tigerstar we're talking about! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3036322564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3036322564" />
    <a title="Historyprincess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess"><img alt="Historyprincess" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3036322564?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Historyprincess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Historyprincess" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess">Historyprincess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30456412-dark-river">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12881308-historyprincess?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3036322564&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3036322564" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer251681043475784744">Premise: Firestar's three grandchildren have all shown great promise since becoming apprentices. But before they know it, each sibling ends up closely guarding a secret from not just their Clan but one another as well. Lionpaw is determined to keep a budding friendship hidden; Hollypaw wonders if she must break the warrior code in order to save it; and Jaypaw finds a link to long-forgotten world in the unlikeliest source. What they have yet to learn is that each secret is tied to the other, and </span>
  <span id="freeText251681043475784744" style="display:none">Premise: Firestar's three grandchildren have all shown great promise since becoming apprentices. But before they know it, each sibling ends up closely guarding a secret from not just their Clan but one another as well. Lionpaw is determined to keep a budding friendship hidden; Hollypaw wonders if she must break the warrior code in order to save it; and Jaypaw finds a link to long-forgotten world in the unlikeliest source. What they have yet to learn is that each secret is tied to the other, and that innocent blood could be shed if knowledge is not shared.<br /><br />Story/Writing: Wow… Who'd have thought that I'd read fifty titles in this series in just two-and-a-half months?! This second installment in the "Power of Three" arc does everything a great sequel should! It ups the drama and the emotions and the characters and everything! With every successive book in every successive arc, these books for me just keep getting better and better! And given how long this series has been going, that's quite an accomplishment. The Erin Hunter team has once again outdone themselves with this title. We essentially follow three different story arcs, each going back and forth with each other. Yet it always feels like it flows smoothly, never needlessly interrupting one of the arcs for no reason, but rather furthering the characters and furthering the story so that all the different parts of the story end up coming together at the end. Not only that, but every time we cut away to a different segment of the story, not once was I disappointed and preferring to get back to another one. I was always interested and wanted to find out where each was ultimately going, and of course how it would all tie together. The conflict and tensions feel real, yet they come from a surprisingly simple source (simple to us as humans, anyway). Not only that, but I particularly liked this book because it raises ideas and questions I've been having in regard to this series for quite a while. That's something I hope they keep up with in the titles I've yet to read because that really drew me in and made the story and conflict feel much more personal.<br /><br />Characters: Speaking of personal, these characters have become so special to me – as I suppose they have to many fans – yet I never get tired of watching them grow and mature before my eyes, so to speak. The ones I'm really familiar with now continue to keep me interested and continue to learn new things. But it's always thrilling getting to know new characters from scratch. I've already become particularly attached to the three siblings. The time spent leading the narrative is more evenly distributed between them this time. As was the case with Squirrelflight and Leafpool, I knew they'd be special from the moment Skywatcher spoke the prophecy to Firestar in his super edition. Each of them feels likable, distinct, and interesting.<br /><br />Lionpaw – Since Lionpaw is on the cover of the version I read, and since it's mainly his story that drives the narrative, I'm gonna consider him the main character. I liked his character in "The Sight," even if he had the least amount of time devoted to him. And while his character development in that book is a bit more straightforward compared to the development his siblings got, he proves himself to be quite a bit more complex this time around. I think I may have mentioned this before in "The Sight," but it's just as true here. You get the sense that ever since they were kits, he's felt this responsibility of looking out for his brother and sister, and not simply because he's the biggest of them. Instead of using his size and strength to bully others, he uses it to protect those he loves and cares about. That said, he does show a bit of a darker side in this book. I thought his friendship with Heatherpaw was cute and sweet, even if they were from different Clans. But you know, they felt like a couple of lovestruck teenagers and I think most of us have had that experience, whether or not it was justified. And while Tigerstar and Hawkfrost do approach him rather suddenly, it does make sense why they would target him. In the previous book, they tried to win over Jaypaw. But when it became clear that he was gonna be a medicine cat and therefore protected from this kind of manipulation by StarClan, it became obvious that they needed easier prey. Hollypaw is far too loyal to the warrior code and what it entails for their taste. So why not go to the ambitious warrior who, in plenty of ways, is like his "father?" And while you do kinda want Lionpaw to remember what he was told about Tigerstar, it also makes sense why he would be drawn to him and willing to learn from him. Tigerstar appeals to Lionpaw's ambitions, and when it's announced at the Gathering in the beginning that Tawnypelt has named one of her new kits Tigerkit, Lionpaw understands why the older cats in attendance get alarmed, but at the same time he doesn't see why Tigerstar's strengths (few though they were) can't be appreciated. In the end though, Lionpaw does prove himself to be a noble and loyal warrior. He takes responsibility for his actions by ending his secret meetings with Heatherpaw and owning up to it all in front of his siblings.<br /><br />Hollypaw – Okay… Currently, Hollypaw has to be probably not only my favorite of the three siblings, but one of my favorite characters in this arc and the series as a whole so far. I connected with her so much in this book, mostly because her personality and beliefs felt very similar to mine. Her story to me was the most intense, not just in terms of what she does but the emotions it brought me as well. She has a very strong sense of right and wrong and has a pretty fierce commitment to the warrior code for her age. But she also knows that sometimes rules have to be broken in order to do the right thing. Granted, I would be lying if I said I thought her sneaking out of ThunderClan to go to see what's wrong with RiverClan by herself was the best idea. But at the same time, I totally understood why she did it. She may be young, but she arguably shows more wisdom than most of the adults do. Firestar and Leafpool dismiss her concerns simply because they believe they have more experience. Not to mention they came across as a bit condescending, however well-intentioned they were. But experience doesn't automatically equal wisdom, and being great doesn't always mean being right. And Hollypaw brings up a great point about how the Clans wouldn't probably need to fight so much if they simply talked things out more. For all they knew, they could've been fighting over nothing. But back to her story, the part where she sneaks off to RiverClan by herself was the most thrilling part of the book to me. And I absolutely felt the crushing weight of the consequences she faces when she gets brought back to ThunderClan and is punished. I felt her anger, resentment, indignation, and frustration – even as I also felt her shame and guilt, 'cause I'd probably feel the same way. In fact, when I got to that part, my brain kind of forced me to read more slowly so I could take in all the intense emotions it got out of me. That said, I was SO happy that she got vindicated in the end!<br /><br />Jaypaw – Jaypaw may be a cranky medicine cat apprentice, but he proves himself to be just as important as his warrior siblings, not in the least because of his special supernatural abilities. I felt almost as intrigued as he did about the stick with the claw marks, mostly because of what happened in the prologue and how much it piqued my interest. When he found the ancient stick, I knew he was eventually gonna discover this secret history. And even though I don't think all of it has been revealed yet, what this book gave me alone in regards to it was very intriguing. But back to Jaypaw's character, while Hollypaw is the sibling I identified with the most, I also identified with him somewhat, mainly because he feels like an introvert and likes his privacy, which is a lot like me. That said, he's also ironically probably the funniest of the siblings. Several things he said in the book got some pretty good laughs out of me. Yet at the same time, I'm glad I got to like his character more since the previous book. Not that I didn't like him before, but he feels like he's grown and learned plenty since he first became an apprentice, even if he still has a lot of room left to mature. His crankiness is still there, but it comes across (in a weird sort of way) as endearing. But while he can be grumpy, as is the case in the last book, he's not gonna leave a cat in distress to suffer, and his siblings are the ones he clearly loves the most. Speaking of which, his grumpiness ironically makes those scenes where he lovingly interacts with his siblings all the more adorable. Like his father (his real father, I mean), he's an intriguing bundle of contradictions.<br /><br />Heatherpaw and Breezepaw – Glad to have some new WindClan cats to get attached to, 'cause I was missing them! I once again thought Heatherpaw was a sweet character, even if she did have her flaws. She is a bit too insistent that Lionpaw keep up his secret meetings with her, yet at the same time, her persistence, the lengths she's willing to go to, and the risks she's willing to take feel kind of admirable in a way. And while she does have a moment of immaturity when Lionpaw "breaks up" with her, and she thinks he simply cares more about being a warrior than about her, I'm willing to let it slip for now 'cause, like I said, they feel like a couple of lovestruck teenagers. That said, she shows great courage when she joins the mission to find the WindClan kits and when she convinces Onestar to spare ThunderClan. As for Breezepaw, my feelings for him are…complicated. Like Jaypaw, he certainly takes after his father, but not always in the best way. He definitely feels like he throws his mouth off just for the sake of it, not to mention he helps to provoke the first fight between ThunderClan and WindClan. But I will give him some credit in that he's willing to accept help from the three siblings, and helps Heatherpaw in stopping Onestar from leading another attack on ThunderClan. He's not the most likable character, but at the very least, he's tolerable. I'm just glad he was written that way on purpose.<br /><br />Leafpool – Out of all the characters from the previous arcs in the series, Leafpool definitely feels the most interesting. I said this before in my review for "The Sight," but it was once again interesting to read this book knowing that she's the real mother of Lionpaw, Hollypaw, and Jaypaw. When you read it with that knowledge in mind, it's easier to pick up hints that are dropped here and there. Yet at the same time, they aren't obvious. For example, when Hollypaw goes missing, Leafpool acts far more concerned than Squirrelflight, if not outright desperate. What's cool is that, for those reading this book not knowing what I know, it could be attributed to the fact that Hollypaw was her first apprentice and therefore pretty special to her. But when you do know what I know as you're reading it, it makes even more sense why she's more emotional about it than Squirrelflight. Not that Squirrelflight isn't concerned, but Leafpool acts quite a bit more like a mother who wants her missing daughter back. With that in mind, while she is a bit overprotective of Cinderpaw when she's injured, it is understandable. This cat is the quote-unquote "reincarnation" (more of my opinion on that in a bit) of her mentor, Cinderpelt. And Cinderpelt only became a medicine cat when she was permanently crippled. So it makes sense that Leafpool wants her to get totally better, even if she is a bit ridiculous about it. That said, while she has become a bit more overly emotional since the "New Prophecy" arc, it never gets to be too much. Her best scene in my opinion is when she and Jaypaw go to speak to Onestar, and she does most of the talking. Not only that, but she does it with such great inner strength and conviction and careful choice of words that you know she means business.<br /><br />Various Other Characters – Out of all the characterizations in this book, the one that surprised me the most was Firestar. I mean that, while he's still a great leader and always will be, he does feel like he's aged quite a bit since the "Prophecies Begin" arc. He still wants to do the right thing and has never felt as though he needed the permission of the other Clan leaders to do what he does, but he also has his Clan and their safety to consider. Now that he's been under that kind of pressure for so long, it's completely understandable why he feels a bit more jaded and even a bit cynical. I don't think he's lost his ideals, but he doesn't have the same amount of enthusiasm he used to have. That's probably why he's dismissive toward Hollypaw at first. Speaking of which, he comes down on her hard when she comes back to face him. I get it, she probably shouldn't have just snuck out on her own like that, and there are certainly worse punishments. Still, it was kind of chilling to see Firestar in a role like that. It definitely shows that the authors are willing to risk making even their best characters a little unlikeable at times. I like to think that what eventually turned him around was that Mousefur reminded him of when he himself went behind Bluestar's back to prevent a battle with WindClan in "A Dangerous Path." It was definitely very similar to what Hollypaw did. Anyway, I'm glad he admitted in the end that she was right. One other character that I think we're all interested in though is Cinderpaw. In my opinion, I don't think it's as simple as saying she's just Cinderpelt reincarnated. For one thing, Cinderpaw doesn't look exactly like Cinderpelt. And while she does have plenty of Cinderpelt's traits, she also has some of her own. From what I know, Cinderpaw's eventual warrior name is also her own – Cinderheart, instead of just Cinderpelt again. That, and Cinderpelt is only awake when Cinderpaw is asleep and vice-versa. I like to think of the two as separate characters, they're just sharing the same body for a time. This is StarClan's way of allowing Cinderpelt to have the experience of becoming the warrior she could've been, had her chance not been stolen from her by Tigerstar when she fell into his trap. Of course, this is all just my opinion. I was also really intrigued by the story of Rock and Fallen Leaves. I knew almost nothing about them going in. But I found their mutual story haunting, and I still have no idea what it could mean and how this connects with the modern Clans. Which is great!<br /><br />Overall: This book was an absolute thrill to read – a very well-constructed plot with great character development. I can't wait to see where the rest of this arc goes and I can't wait to see what roles each of the siblings will play in the prophecy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="251681043475784744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9507233539681072801">Warriors Dark River by Erin Hunter is a really good book. Hollypaw, Lionpaw and Jaypaw are thriving in their apprenticeships. The three of them are unraveling their powers. There are great things about each of their powers, but each of them also discover darkness, in them and in the Clans.<br/></span>

<div id="review_1020005044" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1020005044" />
    <a title="Camille" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25141792-camille"><img alt="Camille" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485793014p2/25141792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1020005044?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camille" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camille" href="/user/show/25141792-camille">Camille</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060892074" href="/book/show/2801574-dark-river">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25141792-camille?shelf=feature">feature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1020005044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14356183934720215591">Dark River is the second book of Warriors: Power of Three. It follows three young cats that live in ThunderClan called Jaypaw, Hollypaw and Lionpaw.<br/><br/>After reading the first of this series, The Sight, I was very keen to start reading this book so I did immediately afterwards. This is where my first praise goes - to the smoothness in which the first book led to the second. I find that many author find it difficult to go into a sequel and a) Provide all the need information and b) Make it seem as is</span>
  <span id="freeText14356183934720215591" style="display:none">Dark River is the second book of Warriors: Power of Three. It follows three young cats that live in ThunderClan called Jaypaw, Hollypaw and Lionpaw.<br /><br />After reading the first of this series, The Sight, I was very keen to start reading this book so I did immediately afterwards. This is where my first praise goes - to the smoothness in which the first book led to the second. I find that many author find it difficult to go into a sequel and a) Provide all the need information and b) Make it seem as is if it really was just a continuation of the first book.Well, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27498.Erin_Hunter" title="Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Erin Hunter</a> did this brilliantly. She provided enough information to give a little catch up of the first book but not too much. Plus it wasn't all at the beginning. During the book I was reminded of things that had happened previously and I was grateful for that.<br /><br />I will try not to repeat anything said in my review for The Sight (link at the bottom) when I talk about the style of the writing but here goes - I really enjoy the different POV's as not only do you understand how the different characters feel about the situation and you also discover the secrets each of these cats have and how they deal with it. It's also nice to know things the other characters don't. Erin Hunter has written in such a brilliant way that you can really believe these characters are absolutely clueless as to what is going on with their clan mates.<br /><br />I have the same praises for the style of writing in my other review so instead of repeating myself I shall talk about the story. This contains spoilers.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tigerstar. I can't believe he's been brought back. I absolutely hated him in the other series and I'm gutted that he's back because I love Lionpaw and I don't want him to go dark side. I also want Lionpaw and Heatherpaw to be together so if she could move her furry ass to ThunderClan I would extremely grateful.<br /><br />And the battles. I'm so glad there were no major ones but I also found it very exciting that Erin Hunter held the fear and anticipation of a battle over our heads and kept it there 'till the last moment. While I do enjoy reading about the cats fighting I find the aftermath of it extremely sad so I'm always grateful when there is no big battle.<br /><br />Also, Millie, Brook and Daisy. I love them but I don't like the fact that they don't have proper warrior names, especially because of all the abuse ThunderClan is getting because of them having 'kittypets' and 'non-clan cats'. So, I really hope that in the next books they change their names.<br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />That is all for now :)<br /> <br />The Sight review -<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1017473249?book_show_action=false">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14356183934720215591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1219240853" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219240853" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6387097-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316662865p2/6387097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219240853?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/6387097-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219240853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14967256445419391871">This series is so far quite intriguing. I can't see how it will end up. Is Jaypaw even one of the 3 with the power of the stars? <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Lionpaw continues his friendship with Heatherpaw and Hollypaw is friends with Willowpaw and both friendships lead towards trouble. Lionpaw gives up Heatherpaw for loyalty to his clan and to be a great warrior. Hollypaw realizes she isn't a medicine cat and can't be friends with Willowpaw anymore (sometimes I wonder if she will end up being medicine cat </span></span>
  <span id="freeText14967256445419391871" style="display:none">This series is so far quite intriguing. I can't see how it will end up. Is Jaypaw even one of the 3 with the power of the stars? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Lionpaw continues his friendship with Heatherpaw and Hollypaw is friends with Willowpaw and both friendships lead towards trouble. Lionpaw gives up Heatherpaw for loyalty to his clan and to be a great warrior. Hollypaw realizes she isn't a medicine cat and can't be friends with Willowpaw anymore (sometimes I wonder if she will end up being medicine cat - afterall Jaypaw doesn't seem to like it much and he's arrogant and there is supposed to be a famous medicine cat with Holly name). Lionpaw and Heatherpaw find an old cave system (guess Heatherpaw could have been a Windclan digger!) and it turns out to have been ritualistically important to a clan of cats that lived around the lake before the four. Jaypaw finds a stick with markings on it by the lake that was a part of the rituals and has dreams about these other ancestors. When Windclan kits go missing they all end up searching for them down in the tunnels with Breezepaw and interestingly Jaypaw feels that the scent of the Darkclan cats is familiar to him (similar to the scents of the cats who lead him to the moonpool) so perhaps it is not Starclan that is so welcoming of him at the moonpool but this other more ancient clan. War of the starclans??? Lets not forget the dark forest cats and Tigerstar and Hawkfrost who have appeared to Jaypaw and are now training Lionpaw. Riverclan has issues with their camp and they almost all end up in battles (for once not caused by Shadowclan) over all of these issues. Hollypaw ends up stuck in Riverclan camp and Squirrelflight has to get her out, but it is Leafpool who is the most anxious about her safety so does that mean that Jaypaw, Hollypaw and Breezepaw are all actually Leafpool's and Crowfeather's? It would appear so and they are all dark pelted. Holly and Breeze are black while Jay is dark gray. Lionpaw is the one that stands out with his golden coat.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Anyways, I am really looking forward to the next books.</span>

<div id="review_1823053868" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1823053868" />
    <a title="Cherie W" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59567088-cherie-w"><img alt="Cherie W" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486503319p2/59567088.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1823053868?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cherie W" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cherie W" href="/user/show/59567088-cherie-w">Cherie W</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59567088-cherie-w?shelf=second-nine-weeks">second-nine-weeks</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1823053868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16464109946474551811">Lionpaw, Hollypaw, and Jaypaw are just like any other apprentice. Lionpaw has a special relationship with Heatherpaw, a Windclan apprentice, and Hollypaw is really suspicious about it. Heatherpaw and Lionpaw meet at night. they don't think their doing anything wrong, but Hollypaw does. So when she and Cinderpaw catch them at it, Heatherpaw finds a cave underground for them to meet in. Through Lionpaw promised himself he would stay loyal to his clan and wouldn't fall behind in his duties, he is l</span>
  <span id="freeText16464109946474551811" style="display:none">Lionpaw, Hollypaw, and Jaypaw are just like any other apprentice. Lionpaw has a special relationship with Heatherpaw, a Windclan apprentice, and Hollypaw is really suspicious about it. Heatherpaw and Lionpaw meet at night. they don't think their doing anything wrong, but Hollypaw does. So when she and Cinderpaw catch them at it, Heatherpaw finds a cave underground for them to meet in. Through Lionpaw promised himself he would stay loyal to his clan and wouldn't fall behind in his duties, he is learning like a slug. His paws are too tired to move, what he hears goes in one ear and out the other. So he gets some extra help from Tigerstar and Hawkfrost. they visit him in dreams, and they encourage his friendship with Heatherpaw. And then Riveclan has a big problem. None of the other clans know what it is, but Onestar keeps pushing at the border with Thunderclan. His Warriors are training to hunt squirrels instead of just rabbits. Riverclan is living on the island. It's really tensioning. And then Hollypaw can't stand it anymore. Firestar won't listen to her. She thinks that if the clans just <i>talked</i> For a little, then they wouldn't have to fight. This battle that is supposedly coming has risen out of gossip and guesswork.She visits Riverclan, and finds out that Riverclan just needs time to solve their problem. She is so mad because she promised Leopardstar that she wouldn't tell anyone about t he problem, and she can't even stop the battle because she promised to hold her tongue! It's infuriating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16464109946474551811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0jKMzLWIqnsCK1b75i8NhFFompcbpT/MoVn5DYUD9zjXPyF6z8CUt4fSB3lqAIsrOE2K5ayTpCny8FGpkPX2nA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZSLLixenICb74uraGjnt0nMYuxC01dfs7hbVFIqk2wdgL2Y9be8e6n4bu1iWFmt9Gj2rYgPjTAm9v32wn1Laow==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Erin Hunter is working on a new series now called Bravelands. <br /><br />Erin Hunter is inspired by a love of cats and a fascination with the ferocity of the natural world. As well as having a great respect for nature in all its forms, Erin enjoys creating rich mythical explanations for animal behavior, shaped by her interest in astronomy and standing stones.</span>
